<div id="review_6926173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6926173" />
    <a title="Stevie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/349251-stevie"><img alt="Stevie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317085360p2/349251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6926173?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stevie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stevie" href="/user/show/349251-stevie">Stevie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349251-stevie?shelf=secular">secular</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6926173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17541898120785267777">Insightful book on the importance of relating well with others and being in tune with one's emotions.<br/><br/>Poignant Quotes:<br/><br/>...childhood and adolescence are critical windows of opportunity for setting down the essential emotional habits that will govern our lives.<br/><br/>...social intelligence is both distinct from academic abilities and a key part of what makes people do well in the practicalities of life.<br/><br/>social competence - how well or poorly people express their own feelings<br/><br/>With a complaint a person critici</span>
  <span id="freeText17541898120785267777" style="display:none">Insightful book on the importance of relating well with others and being in tune with one's emotions.<br /><br />Poignant Quotes:<br /><br />...childhood and adolescence are critical windows of opportunity for setting down the essential emotional habits that will govern our lives.<br /><br />...social intelligence is both distinct from academic abilities and a key part of what makes people do well in the practicalities of life.<br /><br />social competence - how well or poorly people express their own feelings<br /><br />With a complaint a person criticizes the other person's actions. With a personal criticism the person critiques the character/personality of the person.<br /><br />XYZ Method - I feel X when you do Y and I would prefer you to do Z<br /><br />Men also need to be on guard against short-circuiting the discussion by offering a practical solution too early on - it's typically more important to a wife that she feel her husband hears her complaint and empathizes with her feelings about the matter (though he need not agree with her).<br /><br />John Dewey - a moral education is most potent when lessons are taught to children in the course of real events, not just abstract lessons<br /><br />Emotional Self-Awareness<br />-improvement in recognizing and naming own emotions<br />-better able to understand the cause of feelings<br />-recognizing the difference between feelings and actions<br /><br />Managing Emotions<br />-better frustration tolerance and anger management<br />-better able to express anger appropriately<br />-better at handling stress<br />-less loneliness and social anxiety<br /><br />Harnessing Emotions Productively<br />-more responsible<br />-better able to focus on the task at hand and pay attention<br />-less impulsive; more self-control<br /><br />Empathy: Reading Emotions<br />-better able to take another person's perspective<br />-improved empathy and sensitivity to others' feelings<br />-better at listening to others<br /><br />Handling Relationships<br />-Increased ability to analyze and understand relationships<br />-better at resolving conflicts and negotiating disagreements<br />-better at solving problems in relationships<br />-more assertive and skilled in communicating<br />-more sought out by peers<br />-more concerned and considerate<br />-more harmonious in groups<br />-more sharing, cooperation, and helpfulness<br />-more democratic in dealing with others<br /><br />emotion - a feeling and its distinctive thoughts, psychological and biological states, and range of propensities to act<br /><br />In the outer ripples are moods, which, technically speaking, are more muted and last far longer than emotion and beyond moods are temperaments.<br /><br />Some emotions follow from thoughts and others precede or are simultaneous with thought<br /><br />Self-awareness - observing yourself and recognizing your feelings; building a vocabulary for feelings; knowing the relationship between thoughts, feelings, and reactions.<br /><br />Personal decision-making - examining your actions and knowing their consequences; knowing if thought or feeling is ruling a decision; applying these insights to issues such as sex and drugs<br /><br />Managing feelings - monitoring "self-talk" to catch negative messages such as internal put downs; realizing what is behind a feeling (i.e. the hurt that underlies anger); finding ways to handle fears and anxieties, anger, and sadness<br /><br />Handling stress - learning the value of exercise, guided imagery, relaxation methods<br /><br />Empathy - understanding others' feeling and concerns and taking their perspective; appreciating the differences in how people feel about things<br /><br />Communications - talking about feelings effectively; becoming a good listener and question-asker; distinguishing between what someone does or says and your own reactions or judgments about it; sending "I" messages instead of blame<br /><br />Self-disclosure - valuing openness and building trust in a relationship; knowing when it's safe to risk talking about your private feelings<br /><br />Insight - identifying patterns in your emotional life and reactions; recognizing similar patterns in others<br /><br />Self-acceptance - feeling pride and seeing yourself in a positive light; recognizing your strengths and weaknesses; being able to laught at yourself<br /><br />Personal responsibility - taking responsibility; recognizing the consequences of your decisions and actions, accepting your feelings and moods, following through on commitments<br /><br />Assertiveness - stating your concerns and feelings without anger or passivity<br /><br />Group dynamics - cooperation; knowing when and how to lead, when to follow<br /><br />Conflict resolution - how to fight fair; win/win model for negotiating compromise <br /><br />Love others - growing in Emotional Intelligence will help me love people better in a way they feel loved</span>
  <a data-text-id="17541898120785267777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_121314279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121314279" />
    <a title="Lize" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3890298-lize"><img alt="Lize" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501867821p2/3890298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121314279?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lize" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lize" href="/user/show/3890298-lize">Lize</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3890298-lize?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3890298-lize?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3890298-lize?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121314279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7405453776742084210">When I first read this book in 1995--the year it was published--it was required reading for my job in human resources consulting, and I found it amazing and insightful. Fifteen years later it still has some good things to say, but knowing how we've not only ignored Goleman's advice but actually run in the opposite direction (empathy, anyone?) it just made me sad. <br/><br/>The book concerns itself with a key set of characteristics he calls 'emotional intelligence': abilities such as being able to motivate</span>
  <span id="freeText7405453776742084210" style="display:none">When I first read this book in 1995--the year it was published--it was required reading for my job in human resources consulting, and I found it amazing and insightful. Fifteen years later it still has some good things to say, but knowing how we've not only ignored Goleman's advice but actually run in the opposite direction (empathy, anyone?) it just made me sad. <br /><br />The book concerns itself with a key set of characteristics he calls 'emotional intelligence': abilities such as being able to motivate oneself and persist in the face of frustrations; to control impulse and delay gratification; to regulate one's moods and keep distress from swamping the ability to think; to empathize and to hope.<br /><br />This time around I spent the most time on the section about emotional intelligence in marriage (something I had no use for in 1995) and found Dr. John Gottman's research front and center, where it should be. And the "learn to adapt" theory of child rearing he outlines? I really hope that comes back into fashion one day. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7405453776742084210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9653496-hanne?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11884884915645503235">I'm wondering whether this book is perhaps a bit outdated. It is 20 years old, and many of the things we take for granted now might not have been at the time. This book, above anything else, feels like a massive pamphlet to tell us that emotional intelligence is critical. And it shows what happens if we don't have it (either because of brain malfunctioning or bad parenting). <br/><br/>This day and age I think very few people still need convincing that there is such a thing as emotional intelligence; we al</span>
  <span id="freeText11884884915645503235" style="display:none">I'm wondering whether this book is perhaps a bit outdated. It is 20 years old, and many of the things we take for granted now might not have been at the time. This book, above anything else, feels like a massive pamphlet to tell us that emotional intelligence is critical. And it shows what happens if we don't have it (either because of brain malfunctioning or bad parenting). <br /><br />This day and age I think very few people still need convincing that there is such a thing as emotional intelligence; we all know that Sheldon Cooper was at the back of the queue when they were handing it out. And while we love him on our television, we probably would dislike him in real life.<br /><br />Unfortunately i felt that this book wasn't giving me much more than reasons of EQ's existence. But there's nothing really to help you out. Nothing to suggest how to grow it if you feel you're missing a part of it. Nothing to aid you in dealing with low EQ people. Nothing practical in other words, i found it highly theoretical.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11884884915645503235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_11468377'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11468377-thinking-fast-and-slow?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Thinking, Fast and Slow<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/72401.Daniel_Kahneman?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Daniel Kahneman<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.16 avg rating &mdash; 314,794 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2011\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer3845810059440185972\">In the highly anticipated Thinking, Fast and Slow, Kahneman takes us on a groundbreaking tour of the mind and explains the two systems that drive the way we think. System 1 is fast, intuitive, and emotional; System 2 is slower, more deliberative, and<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3845810059440185972\" style=\"display:none\">In the highly anticipated Thinking, Fast and Slow, Kahneman takes us on a groundbreaking tour of the mind and explains the two systems that drive the way we think. System 1 is fast, intuitive, and emotional; System 2 is slower, more deliberative, and more logical. Kahneman exposes the extraordinary capabilities—and also the faults and biases—of fast thinking, and reveals the pervasive influence of intuitive impressions on our thoughts and behavior. The impact of loss aversion and overconfidence on corporate strategies, the difficulties of predicting what will make us happy in the future, the challenges of properly framing risks at work and at home, the profound effect of cognitive biases on everything from playing the stock market to planning the next vacation—each of these can be understood only by knowing how the two systems work together to shape our judgments and decisions.\n\nEngaging the reader in a lively conversation about how we think, Kahneman reveals where we can and cannot trust our intuitions and how we can tap into the benefits of slow thinking. He offers practical and enlightening insights into how choices are made in both our business and our personal lives—and how we can use different techniques to guard against the mental glitches that often get us into trouble. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13515439127531080948">Author of Emotional Intelligence and psychologist Daniel Goleman has transformed the way the world educates children, relates to family and friends, and conducts business. The Wall Street Journal ranked him one of the 10 most influential business thinkers.<br/> <br/>Goleman’s Emotional Intelligence was on The New York Times best sellers list for a year-and-a-half. Named one of the 25 "Most Influential Busin</span>
  <span id="freeText13515439127531080948" style="display:none">Author of Emotional Intelligence and psychologist Daniel Goleman has transformed the way the world educates children, relates to family and friends, and conducts business. The Wall Street Journal ranked him one of the 10 most influential business thinkers.<br /> <br />Goleman’s Emotional Intelligence was on The New York Times best sellers list for a year-and-a-half. Named one of the 25 "Most Influential Business Management Books" by TIME, it has been translated into 40 languages. The Harvard Business Review called emotional intelligence (EI) “a revolutionary, paradigm-shattering idea.” <br /> <br />Goleman’s new book, Focus: The Hidden Driver of Excellence, argues that attention — a fundamental mental ability for success — has come under siege. Leadership that gets results demands a triple focus: on our inner world so we can manage ourselves; on others, for our relationships; and on the outer forces that shape our organizations and society itself. <br /> <br />His more recent books include The Brain and Emotional Intelligence, and Leadership: The Power of Emotional Intelligence - Selected Writings. <br /><br /><br /></span>
